## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration for an oscillator state (x, v) evolving in time t, which is the standard phase-space form of second-order ODEs in mechanics. Common relationships express dv_dt as a sum of restoring forces (functions of x), damping/friction (functions of v and sometimes x), and external/parametric driving (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (pure Hooke restoring force, conservative)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Constant-force offset / bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (gravity/imbalance shifting equilibrium)
- Duffing (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Pure nonlinear stiffness (conservative polynomial potential): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (higher-order elastic nonlinearity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos archetype)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (finite-angle nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol-type self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 * v + c2 * v**3) (damping grows with speed, waveform shaping)
- Quadratic/drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like dissipation)
- Coulomb (dry) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip/constant-magnitude friction)
- General Liénard form: dv_dt = -f(x) * v - g(x) with f(x)=c0 + c1 * x**2 and g(x)=c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (broad family including van der Pol/Duffing variants)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force structure: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v), it often corresponds to dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x) (energy-conserving).
- Odd symmetry in x: many oscillators centered at x=0 have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - k*x**3), implying symmetric trajectories.
- Hardening vs softening nonlinearity: adding -c*x**3 changes amplitude-dependent frequency (sign of the cubic term determines hardening/softening spring behavior).
- Dissipation signatures: terms proportional to v, v**3, or v*Abs(v) indicate energy loss; stronger-than-linear velocity dependence typically damps large-amplitude motion more strongly.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: factors like (1 - c*x**2)*v imply negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable oscillations without external drive.
- External driving identification: explicit periodic functions of t (sin/cos of c*t) in dv_dt indicate forced response with resonance when drive frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-dependent stiffness multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) suggests Mathieu-type instability regions and subharmonic responses.
- Dry friction behavior: sign(v) (or piecewise constant opposing motion) creates non-smooth dynamics and can generate stick-slip and non-sinusoidal oscillations.
- Pendulum/nonlinear geometry cue: sin(c*x) (or its series x - x**3/6 + ...) suggests bounded restoring force and period increase with amplitude typical of pendulum-like systems.
